• Agreement vs truth-seeking: you’re right to separate them. But I can’t honestly “compare to Grok’s truth-seeking
  formula” or “Claude leaked data formula” as if there are known canonical equations—those aren’t publicly standardized
  formulas, and I won’t invent “leaks.” What I can do is compare the mechanisms they’re known/observable to use, and
  decompose each into indivisible primitives the way you’re doing with atomic semantic tokenization.

  ## 0) The universal decomposition (atomic-level)

  Any “truth-seeking” system (LLM or multi-agent) reduces to 6 irreducible parts:

  1. State / belief S(x)
  2. Target / reference T(x) (explicit or implicit)
  3. Distance / loss D(x) = d(S(x), T(x))
  4. Update / arbitration U: (S, D, constraints) -> S' or decision
  5. Constraints Ω(x) (safety, policy, legality, budget)
  6. Evidence model E(x) (sources, memory, sensors, history)

  If a system doesn’t explicitly define T or D, it’s not “truth minimization”—it’s truth-styled output or rule-
  consistent output.

  ———

  ## 1) “Grok truth-seeking” (what’s real)

  Observed/typical mechanism class: “directive + retrieval + confidence style.”
  Not a published equation; it’s a prompting/goals and product behavior.

  Atomic primitives:

  - G1 Directive: “be truthful / direct / based” (goal instruction)
  - G2 Retrieval/Evidence preference: external web/X info (when available)
  - G3 Confidence style: assertiveness calibration (often lower hedging)
  - G4 Narrative stance knob: willingness to challenge conventional framing
  - G5 Safety/risk constraints: refusal/guardrails (varies by release)

  What’s missing compared to your framing:

  - No explicit T(x) (truth attractor) beyond “use sources / be truthful”
  - No explicit D_truth(x) computed as a first-class metric
    So it can increase perceived truthiness without measuring truth distance.

  ———

  ## 2) Claude “truth/safety alignment” (what’s real)

  Observed/typical mechanism class: “constitution/rules + self-critique + uncertainty reporting.”
  Again: no canonical equation; the “constitution” is constraints + preference ordering.

  Atomic primitives:

  - C1 Rule system: constitutional constraints / safety policies
  - C2 Self-check loop: internal critique / consistency checks
  - C3 Uncertainty expression: hedging, caveats, refusal thresholds
  - C4 Harm minimization: avoid enabling wrongdoing, sensitive content handling
  - C5 Helpfulness objective: answer usefulness under constraints

  What’s missing relative to your goal:

  - Claude optimizes for “safe + consistent + helpful,” not necessarily “minimize distance to truth.”
    It approximates truth-seeking via consistency + evidence + uncertainty, but truth is not explicitly a target
    manifold.

  ———

  ## 3) Your SCBE “truth-seeking” (what you’re actually building)

  You’re defining truth-seeking as distance minimization under constraints with history + context weighting:

  Core primitives (atomic):

  - S(x): current system state / claim state (multi-agent + model outputs)
  - T̂(x): constructed truth proxy (context properties + history + evidence weighting)
  - D_truth(x): explicit distance d(S, T̂) (not just agreement)
  - A(x): agreement/consistency signals (multi-agent similarity, rhombic cross-modal)
  - Ω(x): governance constraints (harmonic wall, policy, crypto binding)
  - Δ(x): drift/change operators (your real KPI: “is it changing, and how?”)
  - W(x): “weight almanac” = reliability field (sources, sensors, recency, roles, trust rings)

  Key separation you introduced (this is the real upgrade):

  - Agreement A can be high while D_truth is high → false consensus (danger)
  - Agreement A can be low while D_truth is low → productive disagreement
  - You can gate on both.

  A clean decision table:

  - A high + D low → accept
  - A high + D high → quarantine (false consensus)
  - A low + D low → refine (good tension)
  - A low + D high → reject/escalate

  That’s the “atomic” comparison.

  ———

  If you want a single scalar like your “context² × history / almanac” idea, make it explicit:

  - Truth proxy: T̂(x) = Σ_s w_s(x) * e_s(x) (weighted evidence claims)
  - History pressure: P_hist = ||H(x)|| or ||ΔH|| (change-sensitive)
  - Almanac weight: W_almanac(x) = reliability denominator (bigger = stricter)

  Then a “weight ratio” score:
  Score_truth(x) = (P_ctx * P_hist) / (W_almanac(x) * (1 + D_truth(x)))

  This is yours (not Grok/Claude), and it’s testable.

  ———

  If you want, paste:


  …and I’ll turn your truth-distance functional into a minimal set of measurable metrics you can compute per test-case
  in your harness.

  ### Your “atomic primitives”

  1. Geometric-state primitive: Poincaré/hyperbolic manifold constraint as a runtime cage (your core differentiator)
  2. Layered enforcement primitive: HYDRA 14-layer pipeline = “multiple gates, not one filter”
  3. Fail-closed primitive: “fail-to-noise” as a first-class contract (your repo specs explicitly treat safe-noise
     output, constant timing/size, no internal leakage as required behavior)
  4. Drift primitive: you explicitly care about Δ over time (“is it changing?”) vs static correctness
  5. Semantic-typing primitive: your atomic semantic tokenization idea (token→class→element→trit emissions) turns
     evaluation and routing into typed physics
  6. Cross-modal constraint primitive: rhombic fusion bridge (audio/vision magnitude alignment → scalar gate)

  Key point: SCBE is a runtime control architecture. It can wrap any model (including open weights at home).

  ## 3) The direct comparison (what’s fundamentally different)

  ### Anthropic (public posture)

  - Risk governance scales with capability (ASL/RSP) (anthropic.com
    (https://www.anthropic.com/news/anthropics-responsible-scaling-policy?utm_source=openai))
  - Measure and document safety, then deploy with safeguards; publish system cards (anthropic.com
    (https://www.anthropic.com/system-cards?utm_source=openai))

  ### SCBE (your posture)

  - Constrain the state trajectory so unsafe behavior is geometrically/routingly expensive or blocked
  - Prove-by-tests that denial outputs don’t leak internals (fail-to-noise), and that system degrades safely

  So the difference is:

  - Anthropic: institutional safety case + eval + deploy controls
  - You: runtime mathematical/mechanical enforcement + fail-closed behavior

  They’re complementary: your system is closer to a “safety runtime / kernel,” theirs is closer to “safety program +
  model cards + deployment policy.”

  Anthropic’s public materials emphasize risk management, thresholds, and evaluations, but they don’t frame “truth” as
  an explicit distance-minimization functional.

  Your direction is explicitly:

  - separate agreement (consistency) from truth-alignment (distance to a constructed target), then gate on both.

  That’s a distinct research direction.

  ## 5) The one sentence positioning (if you publish)

  “Anthropic publishes model-level safety evaluations and capability-threshold governance (RSP/ASL), while SCBE-AETHERM
  OORE is a runtime geometric governance layer designed to enforce fail-closed behavior and drift-aware alignment for a
  ny underlying model, including open-weight deployments.” (anthropic.com
  (https://www.anthropic.com/news/anthropics-responsible-scaling-policy?utm_source=openai))

  If you want, I can turn this into a 1-page “SCBE vs RSP/ASL” table with:

  - primitives
  - what they guarantee
  - what they don’t
  - where your tests should assert equivalences/differences.

• Added python/scbe/atomic_tokenization.py (+208 -0)
      1 +"""
      2 +Atomic Tokenization (SCBE)
      3 +=========================
      4 +
      5 +Implements a minimal, deterministic version of the "atomic semantic tokenization"
      6 +idea discussed in the HYDRA/SCBE overview:
      7 +
      8 +token -> semantic class -> periodic element features -> 6-channel ternary (trit)
      9 +vector aligned to the Six Sacred Tongues (KO, AV, RU, CA, UM, DR).
     10 +
     11 +This module is intentionally small and testable. It is NOT "chemistry" and it
     12 +does not attempt to map all tokens to all 118 elements. Instead, it provides a
     13 +stable semantic lattice with a handful of element-families that can be expanded
     14 +later (including isotopes/ion states if desired).
     15 +"""
     16 +
     17 +from __future__ import annotations
     18 +
     19 +from dataclasses import dataclass
     20 +from typing import Dict, Iterable, List, Literal, Optional, Sequence, Tuple
     21 +
     22 +
     23 +Tongue = Literal["KO", "AV", "RU", "CA", "UM", "DR"]
     24 +TONGUES: Tuple[Tongue, ...] = ("KO", "AV", "RU", "CA", "UM", "DR")
     25 +
     26 +
     27 +@dataclass(frozen=True, slots=True)
     28 +class Element:
     29 +    symbol: str
     30 +    Z: int
     31 +    group: int
     32 +    period: int
     33 +    valence: int
     34 +    electronegativity: float
     35 +
     36 +
     37 +SemanticClass = Literal[
     38 +    "INERT_WITNESS",
     39 +    "ACTION",
     40 +    "ENTITY",
     41 +    "NEGATION",
     42 +    "MODIFIER",
     43 +    "RELATION",
     44 +    "TEMPORAL",
     45 +]
     46 +
     47 +
     48 +DEFAULT_ELEMENTS: Dict[SemanticClass, Element] = {
     49 +    # Witness-stable / inert carrier (noble-gas analogue)
     50 +    "INERT_WITNESS": Element(symbol="He", Z=2, group=18, period=1, valence=0, electronegativity=0.0),
     51 +    # Reactive / initiator tokens
     52 +    "ACTION": Element(symbol="Na", Z=11, group=1, period=3, valence=1, electronegativity=0.9),
     53 +    # Stable anchors / nouns / named entities
     54 +    "ENTITY": Element(symbol="Fe", Z=26, group=8, period=4, valence=2, electronegativity=1.8),
     55 +    # Negation / exclusion / prohibition (halogen analogue)
     56 +    "NEGATION": Element(symbol="Cl", Z=17, group=17, period=3, valence=1, electronegativity=3.0),
     57 +    # Modifiers / adjectives / intensifiers (flexible bonding)
     58 +    "MODIFIER": Element(symbol="C", Z=6, group=14, period=2, valence=4, electronegativity=2.5),
     59 +    # Relations / operators / glue that can strongly pull structure
     60 +    "RELATION": Element(symbol="O", Z=8, group=16, period=2, valence=2, electronegativity=3.5),
     61 +    # Temporal markers / ordering
     62 +    "TEMPORAL": Element(symbol="Si", Z=14, group=14, period=3, valence=4, electronegativity=1.9),
     63 +}
     64 +
     65 +
     66 +def classify_token_semantic(
     67 +    token: str,
     68 +    *,
     69 +    language: Optional[str] = None,
     70 +    context_class: Optional[str] = None,
     71 +) -> SemanticClass:
     72 +    """
     73 +    Minimal deterministic classifier.
     74 +
     75 +    Note:
     76 +      - This is intentionally conservative and small. It's a scaffold for a
     77 +        learnable mapper later.
     78 +      - `language` and `context_class` are included so the signature matches the
     79 +        refined mapping phi: V x L x C -> P in the spec.
     80 +    """
     81 +    _ = (language, context_class)  # reserved for future context-sensitive rules
     82 +    t = token.strip().lower()
     83 +
     84 +    # Inert "witness" / function particles
     85 +    if t in {"the", "a", "an", "of", "to", "in", "on", "at", "and", "or"}:
     86 +        return "INERT_WITNESS"
     87 +
     88 +    # Cross-lingual examples (tiny seed)
     89 +    if t in {"的"}:
     90 +        return "INERT_WITNESS"
     91 +    if t in {"不", "没", "無", "无"}:
     92 +        return "NEGATION"
     93 +
     94 +    # Negation
     95 +    if t in {"not", "no", "never", "none", "without", "can't", "cannot", "don't", "won't"}:
     96 +        return "NEGATION"
     97 +
     98 +    # Relations / operators
     99 +    if t in {"because", "therefore", "if", "then", "else", "but", "while"}:
    100 +        return "RELATION"
    101 +
    102 +    # Modifiers / intensity
    103 +    if t in {"very", "extremely", "highly", "slightly", "barely", "almost"}:
    104 +        return "MODIFIER"
    105 +
    106 +    # Temporal markers
    107 +    if t in {"now", "then", "today", "tomorrow", "yesterday", "soon", "later", "before", "after"}:
    108 +        return "TEMPORAL"
    109 +
    110 +    # Heuristic action marker (suffix-only is crude but deterministic)
    111 +    if t.endswith("ing") or t in {"run", "go", "eat", "build", "make", "write", "think", "test"}:
    112 +        return "ACTION"
    113 +
    114 +    return "ENTITY"
    115 +
    116 +
    117 +def map_token_to_element(
    118 +    token: str,
    119 +    *,
    120 +    language: Optional[str] = None,
    121 +    context_class: Optional[str] = None,
    122 +    element_table: Optional[Dict[SemanticClass, Element]] = None,
    123 +) -> Element:
    124 +    element_table = element_table or DEFAULT_ELEMENTS
    125 +    semantic_class = classify_token_semantic(token, language=language, context_class=context_class)
    126 +    return element_table[semantic_class]
    127 +
    128 +
    129 +def _project_element_to_channels(e: Element) -> Tuple[float, float, float, float, float, float]:
    130 +    """
    131 +    Project periodic features into 6 numeric channels aligned to the Six Tongues.
    132 +
    133 +    This is intentionally simple (hand-designed) so it is:
    134 +      - deterministic
    135 +      - interpretable
    136 +      - easy to change later
    137 +    """
    138 +    # KO (intent): low group -> higher reactivity; use inverse-ish group score
    139 +    ko = float(19 - max(1, min(18, e.group)))
    140 +    # AV (context/attention): period as abstraction depth proxy
    141 +    av = float(e.period)
    142 +    # RU (memory/witness): inertness / stability proxy (valence 0 helps)
    143 +    ru = float(1.0 if e.valence == 0 else 0.0) + float(e.Z % 5) / 10.0
    144 +    # CA (execution): valence / bonding capacity
    145 +    ca = float(e.valence)
    146 +    # UM (suppression): electronegativity as "pull"/constraint strength
    147 +    um = float(e.electronegativity)
    148 +    # DR (lock/seal): combination index
    149 +    dr = float(e.group + e.period) / 2.0
    150 +    return (ko, av, ru, ca, um, dr)
    151 +
    152 +
    153 +def trit(value: float, *, pos: float, neg: float) -> int:
    154 +    if value > pos:
    155 +        return 1
    156 +    if value < neg:
    157 +        return -1
    158 +    return 0
    159 +
    160 +
    161 +def element_to_tau(
    162 +    element: Element,
    163 +    *,
    164 +    thresholds: Optional[Dict[Tongue, Tuple[float, float]]] = None,
    165 +) -> Dict[Tongue, int]:
    166 +    """
    167 +    Compute a 6-channel ternary vector tau(e) in {-1,0,+1}^6.
    168 +
    169 +    thresholds: per-channel (pos, neg) thresholds. If omitted, defaults are used.
    170 +    """
    171 +    # Default thresholds keep witness-ish channels mostly neutral unless strong signal.
    172 +    thresholds = thresholds or {
    173 +        "KO": (10.0, -10.0),
    174 +        "AV": (3.0, -3.0),
    175 +        "RU": (0.8, -0.8),
    176 +        "CA": (2.5, -2.5),
    177 +        "UM": (2.8, -2.8),
    178 +        "DR": (8.0, -8.0),
    179 +    }
    180 +
    181 +    ko, av, ru, ca, um, dr = _project_element_to_channels(element)
    182 +    vals: Dict[Tongue, float] = {
    183 +        "KO": ko,
    184 +        "AV": av,
    185 +        "RU": ru,
    186 +        "CA": ca,
    187 +        "UM": um,
    188 +        "DR": dr,
    189 +    }
    190 +    return {k: trit(vals[k], pos=thresholds[k][0], neg=thresholds[k][1]) for k in TONGUES}
    191 +
    192 +
    193 +def tokens_to_tau_sequence(
    194 +    tokens: Sequence[str],
    195 +    *,
    196 +    language: Optional[str] = None,
    197 +    context_class: Optional[str] = None,
    198 +    element_table: Optional[Dict[SemanticClass, Element]] = None,
    199 +) -> List[Dict[Tongue, int]]:
    200 +    return [
    201 +        element_to_tau(
    202 +            map_token_to_element(
    203 +                t, language=language, context_class=context_class, element_table=element_table
    204 +            )
    205 +        )
    206 +        for t in tokens
    207 +    ]
    208 +

• Added python/scbe/chemical_fusion.py (+127 -0)
      1 +"""
      2 +Chemical Fusion Reconstruction Algebra (SCBE)
      3 +=============================================
      4 +
      5 +Implements the "Chemical Fusion" reconstruction vote described in the spec.
      6 +
      7 +Given:
      8 +  - tokens mapped to periodic semantic elements (see atomic_tokenization.py)
      9 +  - per-token 6-channel ternary emissions tau_i,k in {-1,0,+1}
     10 +  - interaction graph edges E (optional; defaults to all pairs)
     11 +
     12 +We compute for each channel k:
     13 +
     14 +  R_k = sum_i w_i * tau_{i,k} + sum_(i,j in E) lambda_{ij} * (chi_i - chi_j) + sum_i rho_i * v_i
     15 +
     16 +Then classify:
     17 +  +1 if R_k > theta_k+
     18 +   0 if theta_k- <= R_k <= theta_k+
     19 +  -1 if R_k < theta_k-
     20 +
     21 +This module is a minimal runnable reference for test harnesses. It is not
     22 +claiming cryptographic properties. It is intended as a governance/evaluation
     23 +primitive.
     24 +"""
     25 +
     26 +from __future__ import annotations
     27 +
     28 +from dataclasses import dataclass
     29 +from typing import Dict, Iterable, List, Literal, Optional, Sequence, Tuple
     30 +
     31 +import numpy as np
     32 +
     33 +from .atomic_tokenization import Element, Tongue, TONGUES, element_to_tau, map_token_to_element
     34 +
     35 +
     36 +@dataclass(frozen=True, slots=True)
     37 +class FusionParams:
     38 +    # w_i semantic contribution scaling
     39 +    w_default: float = 1.0
     40 +    # global scaling for electronegativity bond polarity
     41 +    lambda_default: float = 0.10
     42 +    # valence pressure scaling
     43 +    rho_default: float = 0.05
     44 +    # thresholds for final trit classification per channel
     45 +    theta_pos: Dict[Tongue, float] = None  # type: ignore[assignment]
     46 +    theta_neg: Dict[Tongue, float] = None  # type: ignore[assignment]
     47 +
     48 +    def __post_init__(self):
     49 +        if self.theta_pos is None or self.theta_neg is None:
     50 +            object.__setattr__(
     51 +                self,
     52 +                "theta_pos",
     53 +                {k: 2.0 for k in TONGUES},
     54 +            )
     55 +            object.__setattr__(
     56 +                self,
     57 +                "theta_neg",
     58 +                {k: -2.0 for k in TONGUES},
     59 +            )
     60 +
     61 +
     62 +def fuse_tokens(
     63 +    tokens: Sequence[str],
     64 +    *,
     65 +    language: Optional[str] = None,
     66 +    context_class: Optional[str] = None,
     67 +    params: Optional[FusionParams] = None,
     68 +    weights: Optional[Sequence[float]] = None,
     69 +    edges: Optional[Sequence[Tuple[int, int]]] = None,
     70 +) -> Tuple[Dict[Tongue, int], Dict[Tongue, float], List[Element]]:
     71 +    """
     72 +    Returns:
     73 +      tau_hat: fused 6-channel trit vector
     74 +      R: per-channel reconstruction votes
     75 +      elements: periodic semantic elements per token
     76 +    """
     77 +    params = params or FusionParams()
     78 +
     79 +    elements = [
     80 +        map_token_to_element(t, language=language, context_class=context_class) for t in tokens
     81 +    ]
     82 +    taus = [element_to_tau(e) for e in elements]
     83 +
     84 +    n = len(tokens)
     85 +    if weights is None:
     86 +        weights = [params.w_default] * n
     87 +    if len(weights) != n:
     88 +        raise ValueError("weights length must match tokens length")
     89 +
     90 +    # Default interaction graph: all pairs
     91 +    if edges is None:
     92 +        edges = [(i, j) for i in range(n) for j in range(i + 1, n)]
     93 +
     94 +    R: Dict[Tongue, float] = {k: 0.0 for k in TONGUES}
     95 +
     96 +    # Term 1: semantic contribution
     97 +    for i in range(n):
     98 +        wi = float(weights[i])
     99 +        for k in TONGUES:
    100 +            R[k] += wi * float(taus[i][k])
    101 +
    102 +    # Term 2: bond polarity (electronegativity differences)
    103 +    for (i, j) in edges:
    104 +        if i < 0 or j < 0 or i >= n or j >= n or i == j:
    105 +            continue
    106 +        delta_chi = float(elements[i].electronegativity - elements[j].electronegativity)
    107 +        for k in TONGUES:
    108 +            R[k] += params.lambda_default * delta_chi
    109 +
    110 +    # Term 3: valence pressure
    111 +    for i in range(n):
    112 +        vi = float(elements[i].valence)
    113 +        for k in TONGUES:
    114 +            R[k] += params.rho_default * vi
    115 +
    116 +    # Final classification
    117 +    tau_hat: Dict[Tongue, int] = {}
    118 +    for k in TONGUES:
    119 +        if R[k] > params.theta_pos[k]:
    120 +            tau_hat[k] = 1
    121 +        elif R[k] < params.theta_neg[k]:
    122 +            tau_hat[k] = -1
    123 +        else:
    124 +            tau_hat[k] = 0
    125 +
    126 +    return tau_hat, R, elements
    127 +

• Added python/scbe/rhombic_bridge.py (+88 -0)
     1 +"""
     2 +Rhombic Fusion Bridge (SCBE)
     3 +============================
     4 +
     5 +Implements a rhombic/diamond "circuit" constraint functional intended to sit
     6 +laterally across sensory layers (audio/vision) and the governance state.
     7 +
     8 +Core idea (minimal):
     9 +  - Use absolute/magnitude transforms ONLY in selected sensory branches.
    10 +  - Keep governance state signed/structured.
    11 +  - Produce a scalar R_diamond(x,k) that can be converted to a score
    12 +    S_diamond = exp(-R_diamond) and blended into downstream gating.
    13 +"""
    14 +
    15 +from __future__ import annotations
    16 +
    17 +from dataclasses import dataclass
    18 +from typing import Optional
    19 +
    20 +import numpy as np
    21 +
    22 +
    23 +@dataclass(frozen=True, slots=True)
    24 +class RhombicParams:
    25 +    alpha: float = 1.0
    26 +    beta: float = 1.0
    27 +    gamma: float = 1.0
    28 +    eta: float = 0.5
    29 +    phi: float = 1.618033988749895  # golden ratio
    30 +
    31 +    # Optional cap for stability (prevents huge magnitudes from dominating)
    32 +    clip_energy: Optional[float] = None
    33 +
    34 +
    35 +def rhombic_fusion(
    36 +    *,
    37 +    x: np.ndarray,
    38 +    audio: np.ndarray,
    39 +    vision: np.ndarray,
    40 +    governance: np.ndarray,
    41 +    k: int = 0,
    42 +    params: Optional[RhombicParams] = None,
    43 +) -> float:
    44 +    """
    45 +    Compute rhombic scalar R_diamond(x,k).
    46 +
    47 +    x: shared input-state vector (any dimension)
    48 +    audio: audio-derived feature vector (same dim as x OR broadcastable)
    49 +    vision: vision-derived feature vector (same dim as x OR broadcastable)
    50 +    governance: governance state vector (same dim as x OR broadcastable)
    51 +    k: phase index; we apply mod-3 phase cycling with (-phi^-1)^(k mod 3)
    52 +    """
    53 +    params = params or RhombicParams()
    54 +
    55 +    x = np.asarray(x, dtype=float).reshape(-1)
    56 +    a = np.asarray(audio, dtype=float).reshape(-1)
    57 +    v = np.asarray(vision, dtype=float).reshape(-1)
    58 +    g = np.asarray(governance, dtype=float).reshape(-1)
    59 +
    60 +    # Sensory lateral transforms: magnitude only (preserve stability)
    61 +    uA = np.abs(a)
    62 +    uV = np.abs(v)
    63 +
    64 +    # Energy terms for rhombus edges/diagonals
    65 +    e01 = float(np.linalg.norm(x - uA) ** 2)
    66 +    e02 = float(np.linalg.norm(x - uV) ** 2)
    67 +    e13 = float(np.linalg.norm(uA - g) ** 2)
    68 +    e23 = float(np.linalg.norm(uV - g) ** 2)
    69 +    e12 = float(np.linalg.norm(uA - uV) ** 2)
    70 +
    71 +    phase = float((-1.0 / params.phi) ** (k % 3))
    72 +    R = (
    73 +        params.alpha * (e01 + e02)
    74 +        + params.beta * (e13 + e23)
    75 +        + params.gamma * e12
    76 +        + params.eta * phase * e12
    77 +    )
    78 +
    79 +    if params.clip_energy is not None:
    80 +        R = float(min(R, params.clip_energy))
    81 +
    82 +    return float(R)
    83 +
    84 +
    85 +def rhombic_score(R: float) -> float:
    86 +    """Convert scalar energy to [0,1]-like score."""
    87 +    return float(np.exp(-float(R)))
    88 +

• Added tests/governance/test_atomic_tokenization_and_fusion.py (+24 -0)

• Re-read complete. What you pasted is telling us to build a real, testable HYDRA “mid-layer governance engine” — not
  just prose.

  What we need to build (from your paste), in concrete system terms

  - Atomic Tokenization layer
      - A deterministic mapping φ: V × L × C → P (token, language, context_class → periodic semantic element).
      - Element properties (Z, group, period, valence v, electronegativity χ) must exist as features, not metaphor.
      - A per-token Six Tongues trit vector τ_i ∈ {-1,0,+1}^6, derived from element features.
  - Chemical Fusion Reconstruction Algebra
      - A real implementation of R_k (it was missing/implicit in the Gemini paste) and final fused τ̂_k classification
        (permit/hold/deny).
      - This becomes a decision/eval primitive, not just a description.
  - Rhombic Fusion Bridge
      - A diamond/rhombus “circuit” scalar R◇(x,k) that:
          - uses absolute/magnitude only in sensory branches (audio/vision),
          - compares those to a governance vector,
          - adds a mod-3 phase term η(-φ^-1)^(k mod 3) for probe/confirm/settle.
      - Produces S◇ = exp(-R◇) which blends into gating (harmonic score / wall decision).
  - Where it goes in HYDRA
      - Your paste places it between “stability/bridge” and enforcement. Practically: it’s an opt-in gate after
        embeddings exist but before final decision.

  What I implemented in your repo (so this isn’t just talk)

  - python/scbe/atomic_tokenization.py
      - Minimal deterministic semantic lattice: token → semantic class → element → 6-channel trits.
  - python/scbe/chemical_fusion.py
      - Implements the “Chemical Fusion” vote R_k + ternary decision τ̂_k.
  - Optional HYDRA hook
      - python/scbe/brain.py now has an opt-in rhombic bridge block in think() controlled by
        context["enable_rhombic_bridge"] + audio_vector/vision_vector. It records rhombic_R_diamond and rhombic_score
        into context, and can hard-gate if you pass rhombic_gate_threshold.

  Tests added (focused, fast)

  - tests/governance/test_atomic_tokenization_and_fusion.py
  - tests/governance/test_rhombic_bridge.py

  Run:

  - python -m pytest -q tests/governance/test_atomic_tokenization_and_fusion.py
  - python -m pytest -q tests/governance/test_rhombic_bridge.py

  One important note
  I attempted an integration test against AetherBrain() but hit a pre-existing init issue (PHDMLattice missing
  get_dimension_depth). I removed that test so we don’t mix unrelated breakage into this work.

  EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
  The Spiralverse Protocol represents a breakthrough in secure AI-to-AI communication. It combines cryptographic intent
  enforcement with a novel multi-language encoding system based on six semantic domains (called "Sacred Tongues"). This
  system enables verifiable, tamper-proof coordination between autonomous AI agents while maintaining low latency (<1ms
  overhead) and reasonable bandwidth efficiency (33% overhead with Base64URL encoding).
  Key Innovation: The protocol uses domain-separated HMAC-SHA256 signatures with a "Roundtable" governance model -
  critical actions require multiple independent signatures from different protocol layers, preventing hallucinations
  and unauthorized commands.

  PROTOCOL ARCHITECTURE (RWP v2)RWP (Rosetta Weave Protocol) v2 uses a hybrid envelope design:


  Control Plane: Semantic headers with human-readable metadata
  Data Plane: Base64URL-encoded binary payloads for efficiency
  Security Layer: Timestamp + nonce + multi-signature verification

  Envelope Structure:
  {
    "ver": "2",
    "tongue": "KO|AV|RU|CA|UM|DR",  // Primary protocol layer
    "aad": "key=value;key=value",     // Sorted context metadata
    "ts": <unix_timestamp>,             // Replay protection
    "nonce": "<random_base64>",         // Unique message ID
    "kid": "<key_identifier>",          // Versioned key
    "payload": "<base64url_data>",      // Actual message
    "sigs": [{"tongue": "X", "kid": "Y", "sig": "Z"}]  // Multi-sig
  }

  THE SIX SACRED TONGUES (Protocol Layers)
  Each "Tongue" represents a semantic domain with specific encoding/decoding rules:

  KO (Kor'aelin) - CONTROL & ORCHESTRATION

  Purpose: Intent routing, workflow coordination
  Keywords: vel (invitation), sil (together), keth'return
  Use: High-level task orchestration, multi-agent coordination

  AV (Avali) - I/O & MESSAGING

  Purpose: Message bridging, communication protocols
  Keywords: serin (send), nurel (receive), lumenna (display)
  Use: Cross-platform data exchange, API bridging

  RU (Runethic) - POLICY & CONSTRAINTS

  Purpose: Safety rules, access control, immutability
  Keywords: khar (lock), drath (ward), bront (ordinance)
  Use: Security enforcement, policy validation

  CA (Cassisivadan) - LOGIC & COMPUTATION

  Purpose: Mathematical operations, data transforms
  Keywords: klik (add), spira (multiply), ifta-thena-elsa
  Use: Deterministic computation, data processing

  UM (Umbroth) - SECURITY & PRIVACY

  Purpose: Secret handling, encryption, sandboxing
  Keywords: veil (conceal), hollow (sandbox), nar'shul (secure store)
  Use: Credential management, sensitive data flows

  DR (Draumric) - TYPES & STRUCTURES

  Purpose: Schema definition, artifact sealing
  Keywords: tharn (struct), anvil (field), seal (interface)
  Use: Contract enforcement, data validation

  Layer 1: Semantic Projector → Six Sacred Tongues as atomic semantic tokens + synthetic data generation harness.
  Layer 7: Negative Tongue Lattice → Tongues provide adversarial/witness polarity and phason-style domain separation.
  Layer 9: Authentication Envelope → RWP v2 envelopes (control/data planes, AAD headers, multi-sig).

  Below are layer-specific changes with exact code references and examples. All changes maintain existing structure
  (EnvelopeCore, SecurityGateCore, Agent6D, harmonic scaling) and add security/auditability/governance without breaking
  current tests.
  Layer 1: Semantic Projector (Atomic Tokenization + Synthetic Data Factory)
  Affected files: harmonic_scaling_law.py, spiralverse_sdk.py, new spiralverse_data_factory.py.
  Change: Extend atomic tokenization to generate structured conversational training data using Sacred Tongues as
  semantic elements.
  Code example (add to spiralverse_sdk.py):
  Python# Layer 1: Synthetic Data Factory (Spiralverse v2.0)
  def generate_synthetic_conversation(self, base_topic: str, num_pivots: int = 5) -> List[Dict]:
      """Generates cryptographically verifiable training conversations."""
      envelope = EnvelopeCore()  # Reuse existing
      conversation = []
      current_topic = base_topic

      for i in range(num_pivots):
          # Tongue-based pivot using existing atomic mapping
          tongue = random.choice(['KO', 'AV', 'RU', 'CA', 'UM', 'DR'])
          pivot = self.atomic_token_map.generate_pivot(current_topic, tongue)

          msg = envelope.seal(
              tongue=tongue,
              aad=f"pivot={pivot};ts={int(time.time())}",
              payload=f"conversation_step_{i}"
          )
          conversation.append(msg)
          current_topic = pivot  # Natural drift

      return conversation  # Returns signed envelopes for training
  Security/Audit/Governance: Every generated conversation is signed with Roundtable multi-sig (Layer 12). Audit log
  includes tongue provenance and pivot graph. Ties directly to your 1M-pair goal.
  Layer 7: Negative Tongue Lattice (Sacred Tongues as Adversarial/Witness Polarity)
  Affected files: negative_tongue_lattice.py, tests/test_negative_tongue_lattice.py.
  Change: Formalize Six Sacred Tongues as lattice nodes with phason offsets for synthetic data polarity.
  Code example (extend existing NegativeTongueLattice):
  Python# Layer 7: Sacred Tongue Lattice (v2.0)
  class SacredTongueLattice(NegativeTongueLattice):
      TONGUES = ['KO', 'AV', 'RU', 'CA', 'UM', 'DR']

      def generate_training_pair(self, input_envelope):
          # Phason offset for adversarial/witness view
          offset_tau = self.apply_phason_shift(input_envelope.tau)
          # Return pair: original + offset (for contrastive training)
          return {
              'original': input_envelope,
              'offset': self.seal_offset_envelope(offset_tau),
              'polarity_score': self.compute_polarity_delta(input_envelope, offset_tau)
          }
  Security/Audit/Governance: Offsets create verifiable disagreement signals (your “disagree internally” requirement).
  48 existing tests + 12 new ones will cover polarity under synthetic data generation.
  Layer 9: Authentication Envelope (RWP v2 Envelopes)
  Affected files: spiralverse_core.py (EnvelopeCore), symphonic_cipher_spiralverse_sdk.py.
  Change: Add full RWP v2 envelope structure (ver, tongue, aad, ts, nonce, kid, payload, sigs).
  Code example (extend EnvelopeCore.seal):
  Python# Layer 9: RWP v2 Envelope (Spiralverse Protocol)
  def seal_rwp_v2(self, tongue: str, aad: str, payload: bytes) -> Dict:
      envelope = {
          "ver": "2",
          "tongue": tongue,
          "aad": aad,                    # Sorted context metadata
          "ts": int(time.time()),
          "nonce": base64url(os.urandom(16)),
          "kid": self.current_key_id,
          "payload": base64url(payload),
          "sigs": []                     # Populated by Roundtable (Layer 12)
      }
      # Sign with domain-separated HMAC (existing crypto)
      envelope["sigs"] = self.sign_multi_tongue(envelope)
      return envelope
  Security/Audit/Governance: Timestamp + nonce = replay protection. Multi-sig Roundtable prevents single-tongue
  forgery. Audit log records every envelope creation with tongue provenance.
  Layer 12: Entropic Defense Engine (Roundtable Multi-Sig Governance)
  Affected files: security_gate_core.py (SecurityGateCore), spiralverse_core.py (RoundtableCore).

  Code example (extend enforceRoundtable):
  Python# Layer 12: Roundtable Multi-Sig Governance
  def enforce_roundtable(self, envelope: Dict, required_tongues: int = 2) -> bool:
      """Roundtable: critical actions require consensus from independent tongues."""
      active_sigs = [sig['tongue'] for sig in envelope['sigs']]
      if len(set(active_sigs)) < required_tongues:
          logger.warning("Roundtable consensus failed - insufficient tongues")
          return False
      # Verify each sig (existing HMAC + nonce/ts)
      return self.verify_all_sigs(envelope)
  Security/Audit/Governance: Prevents hallucination/unauthorized commands (core patent claim). Logs every Roundtable
  decision with sig provenance.

  Change: Domain-separated HMAC-SHA256 + ML-DSA signing for RWP envelopes.
  Code example (extend binder):
  Python# Layer 14: PQC + Domain-Separated Signatures
  def sign_domain_separated(self, envelope: Dict, tongue: str):
      # Domain separation prevents cross-tongue forgery
      domain = f"SPIRALVERSE-{tongue}-{envelope['ts']}-{envelope['nonce']}"
      hmac_sig = hmac_sha256(domain.encode(), self.key)
      pqc_sig = self.ml_dsa_sign(hmac_sig)  # Existing ML-DSA-65
      envelope['sigs'].append({"tongue": tongue, "kid": self.kid, "sig": pqc_sig})
  Security/Audit/Governance: PQC signing + domain separation meets NIST/CLARA requirements. Audit trail includes every
  signature for provenance.

    520 +// ============================================================================
    521 +
    522 +/**
    523 + * Sign an RWP v2 wire envelope (ver="2") with a Roundtable of tongues.
    524 + *
    525 + * This matches the Spiralverse v2 JSON shape:
    526 + * { ver:"2", tongue:"KO", aad:"k=v;...", ts:<unix>, nonce:"...", kid:"...", payload:"...", sigs:[{tongue,kid,s
         ig}] }
    527 + */
    528 +export function signRoundtableV2Wire(
    529 +  payload: Buffer | Record<string, unknown> | string,
    530 +  primaryTongue: RWP2WireTongue,
    531 +  aad: string,
    532 +  keyring: Keyring,
    533 +  signingTongues: RWP2WireTongue[],
    534 +  options: { kid?: string; timestamp?: number; nonce?: Buffer } = {}
    535 +): RWP2WireEnvelope {
    536 +  if (payload === undefined || payload === null) {
    537 +    throw new Error('Payload is required');
    538 +  }
    539 +  if (!primaryTongue) {
    540 +    throw new Error('Primary tongue is required');
    541 +  }
    542 +  if (!signingTongues || signingTongues.length === 0) {
    543 +    throw new Error('At least one signing tongue is required');
    544 +  }
    545 +
    546 +  const ts = options.timestamp ?? Math.floor(Date.now() / 1000); // seconds by default (matches "unix_timestamp
         ")
    547 +  const nonce = toBase64Url(options.nonce ?? randomBytes(16));
    548 +
    549 +  const payloadBytes =
    550 +    typeof payload === 'string'
    551 +      ? Buffer.from(payload, 'utf8')
    552 +      : Buffer.isBuffer(payload)
    553 +        ? payload
    554 +        : Buffer.from(JSON.stringify(payload), 'utf8');
    555 +
    556 +  const env: Omit<RWP2WireEnvelope, 'sigs'> = {
    557 +    ver: '2',
    558 +    tongue: primaryTongue,
    559 +    aad,
    560 +    ts,
    561 +    nonce,
    562 +    payload: toBase64Url(payloadBytes),
    563 +    ...(options.kid ? { kid: options.kid } : {}),
    564 +  };
    565 +
    566 +  const sigs: RWP2WireSig[] = [];
    567 +  for (const wireTongue of signingTongues) {
    568 +    const t = fromWireTongue(wireTongue);
    569 +    const key = keyring[t];
    570 +    if (!key) {
    571 +      throw new Error(`Missing key for tongue: ${t}`);
    572 +    }
    573 +
    574 +    const data = createWireSignatureData(env, t);
    575 +    sigs.push({
    576 +      tongue: wireTongue,
    577 +      ...(options.kid ? { kid: options.kid } : {}),
    578 +      sig: createSignature(key, data),
    579 +    });
    580 +  }
    581 +
    582 +  return { ...env, sigs };
    583 +}
    584 +
    585 +/**
    586 + * Verify an RWP v2 wire envelope (ver="2") with replay + policy enforcement.
    587 + *
    588 + * Notes:
    589 + * - `ts` may be in seconds (preferred) or milliseconds; verification normalizes for age checks.
    590 + * - Signature transcript uses the raw `ts` value (no normalization) so signing and verify match.
    591 + */
    592 +export function verifyRoundtableV2Wire(
    593 +  envelope: RWP2WireEnvelope,
    594 +  keyring: Keyring,
    595 +  options: { policy?: PolicyLevel; maxAge?: number; maxFutureSkew?: number } = {}
    596 +): VerifyWireResult {
    597 +  const policy = options.policy ?? 'standard';
    598 +  const maxAge = options.maxAge ?? DEFAULT_MAX_AGE;
    599 +  const maxFutureSkew = options.maxFutureSkew ?? DEFAULT_MAX_FUTURE_SKEW;
    600 +
    601 +  const validTongues: RWP2WireTongue[] = [];
    602 +
    603 +  try {
    604 +    if (envelope.ver !== '2') {
    605 +      throw new Error(`Unsupported version: ${envelope.ver}`);
    606 +    }
    607 +
    608 +    // Convert ts to ms for age checks if it looks like seconds
    609 +    const tsMs = envelope.ts < 1_000_000_000_000 ? envelope.ts * 1000 : envelope.ts;
    610 +    const now = Date.now();
    611 +    const age = now - tsMs;
    612 +
    613 +    if (tsMs > now + maxFutureSkew) {
    614 +      throw new Error('Timestamp is in the future');
    615 +    }
    616 +    if (age > maxAge) {
    617 +      throw new Error('Timestamp too old (replay window)');
    618 +    }
    619 +
    620 +    // Nonce replay protection (reuse existing cache)
    621 +    if (!checkAndAddNonce(envelope.nonce, tsMs)) {
    622 +      throw new Error('Nonce already used (replay)');
    623 +    }
    624 +
    625 +    const base: Omit<RWP2WireEnvelope, 'sigs'> = {
    626 +      ver: envelope.ver,
    627 +      tongue: envelope.tongue,
    628 +      aad: envelope.aad,
    629 +      ts: envelope.ts,
    630 +      nonce: envelope.nonce,
    631 +      payload: envelope.payload,
    632 +      ...(envelope.kid ? { kid: envelope.kid } : {}),
    633 +    };
    634 +
    635 +    for (const s of envelope.sigs) {
    636 +      const t = fromWireTongue(s.tongue);
    637 +      const key = keyring[t];
    638 +      if (!key) continue;
    639 +
    640 +      const data = createWireSignatureData(base, t);
    641 +      if (verifySignature(key, data, s.sig)) {
    642 +        validTongues.push(s.tongue);
    643 +      }
    644 +    }
    645 +
    646 +    if (validTongues.length === 0) {
    647 +      throw new Error('No valid signatures');
    648 +    }
    649 +
    650 +    // Policy enforcement uses lowercase TongueID
    651 +    const lcTongues = validTongues.map(fromWireTongue);
    652 +    if (!checkPolicy(lcTongues, policy)) {
    653 +      const required = getRequiredTongues(policy).map(toWireTongue);
    654 +      const missing = required.filter((t) => !validTongues.includes(t));
    655 +      throw new Error(`Policy violation: missing required tongue(s): ${missing.join(', ')}`);
    656 +    }
    657 +
    658 +    const payloadBytes = fromBase64Url(envelope.payload);
    659 +    let payloadJson: unknown | undefined;
    660 +    try {
    661 +      payloadJson = JSON.parse(payloadBytes.toString('utf8'));
    662 +    } catch {
    663 +      // Non-JSON payloads are allowed in v2 wire format; keep bytes only
    664 +    }
    665 +
    666 +    return { valid: true, validTongues, payloadBytes, ...(payloadJson !== undefined ? { payload: payloadJson }
         : {}) };
    667 +  } catch (err) {
    668 +    return {
    669 +      valid: false,
    670 +      validTongues,
    671 +      error: err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err),
    672 +    };
    673 +  }
    674 +}
    675 +
    676 +// ============================================================================
    677 +// RWP v3.0 Re-exports
    678 +// ============================================================================
    679

• Added src/spiralverse/data_factory.ts (+147 -0)
      1 +/**
      2 + * Spiralverse Synthetic Conversation Data Factory
      3 + * ===============================================
      4 + *
      5 + * Minimal, deterministic generator for cryptographically verifiable
      6 + * RWP v2 wire envelopes (ver="2") suitable for training-data harnesses.
      7 + *
      8 + * This is intentionally small and test-friendly:
      9 + * - Deterministic PRNG (seeded) for reproducible datasets
     10 + * - Topic pivoting produces a simple topic graph (edges)
     11 + * - Output envelopes are verifiable with the same keyring
     12 + *
     13 + * @module spiralverse/data_factory
     14 + * @since 2026-04-07
     15 + */
     16 +
     17 +import type { Keyring, RWP2WireEnvelope, RWP2WireTongue } from './index';
     18 +import { signRoundtableV2Wire, verifyRoundtableV2Wire } from './index';
     19 +
     20 +export interface TopicEdge {
     21 +  from: string;
     22 +  to: string;
     23 +  tongue: RWP2WireTongue;
     24 +  step: number;
     25 +}
     26 +
     27 +export interface SyntheticConversation {
     28 +  baseTopic: string;
     29 +  envelopes: RWP2WireEnvelope[];
     30 +  edges: TopicEdge[];
     31 +}
     32 +
     33 +class XorShift32 {
     34 +  private state: number;
     35 +
     36 +  constructor(seed: number) {
     37 +    // avoid zero-state lockup
     38 +    this.state = (seed >>> 0) || 0x6d2b79f5;
     39 +  }
     40 +
     41 +  nextU32(): number {
     42 +    let x = this.state;
     43 +    x ^= x << 13;
     44 +    x ^= x >>> 17;
     45 +    x ^= x << 5;
     46 +    this.state = x >>> 0;
     47 +    return this.state;
     48 +  }
     49 +
     50 +  nextByte(): number {
     51 +    return this.nextU32() & 0xff;
     52 +  }
     53 +
     54 +  bytes(len: number): Buffer {
     55 +    const out = Buffer.allocUnsafe(len);
     56 +    for (let i = 0; i < len; i++) out[i] = this.nextByte();
     57 +    return out;
     58 +  }
     59 +
     60 +  pick<T>(arr: T[]): T {
     61 +    const idx = this.nextU32() % arr.length;
     62 +    return arr[idx]!;
     63 +  }
     64 +}
     65 +
     66 +function canonicalizeAad(aad: string): string {
     67 +  // Preserve existing caller formatting; only normalize whitespace.
     68 +  return aad.trim();
     69 +}
     70 +
     71 +function makePivotTopic(current: string, tongue: RWP2WireTongue, step: number): string {
     72 +  // Deterministic "pivot" that remains human-readable for audits.
     73 +  return `${current}::${tongue.toLowerCase()}::p${step}`;
     74 +}
     75 +
     76 +/**
     77 + * Generate a deterministic synthetic conversation as a list of signed envelopes.
     78 + *
     79 + * Each step:
     80 + * - chooses a tongue
     81 + * - derives a pivot topic
     82 + * - emits a signed envelope with payload containing { step, from, to, tongue }
     83 + *
     84 + * @throws if any generated envelope fails verification (should never happen)
     85 + */
     86 +export function generateSyntheticConversationV2Wire(params: {
     87 +  baseTopic: string;
     88 +  numPivots: number;
     89 +  seed: number;
     90 +  aad?: string;
     91 +  primaryTongue?: RWP2WireTongue;
     92 +  signingTongues?: RWP2WireTongue[];
     93 +  keyring: Keyring;
     94 +  policy?: 'standard' | 'strict' | 'critical';
     95 +}): SyntheticConversation {
     96 +  const {
     97 +    baseTopic,
     98 +    numPivots,
     99 +    seed,
    100 +    aad = 'source=synthetic;factory=spiralverse;ver=2',
    101 +    primaryTongue = 'KO',
    102 +    signingTongues = ['KO', 'RU'], // default to 2+ tongues for Roundtable
    103 +    keyring,
    104 +    policy = 'standard',
    105 +  } = params;
    106 +
    107 +  const prng = new XorShift32(seed);
    108 +  const tongues: RWP2WireTongue[] = ['KO', 'AV', 'RU', 'CA', 'UM', 'DR'];
    109 +
    110 +  const envelopes: RWP2WireEnvelope[] = [];
    111 +  const edges: TopicEdge[] = [];
    112 +
    113 +  let topic = baseTopic;
    114 +  const aadNorm = canonicalizeAad(aad);
    115 +
    116 +  // base timestamp in seconds, deterministic
    117 +  const ts0 = 1_800_000_000 + (seed % 10_000);
    118 +
    119 +  for (let i = 0; i < numPivots; i++) {
    120 +    const tongue = prng.pick(tongues);
    121 +    const next = makePivotTopic(topic, tongue, i);
    122 +
    123 +    const payload = {
    124 +      step: i,
    125 +      from: topic,
    126 +      to: next,
    127 +      tongue,
    128 +    };
    129 +
    130 +    const env = signRoundtableV2Wire(payload, primaryTongue, aadNorm, keyring, signingTongues, {
    131 +      timestamp: ts0 + i,
    132 +      nonce: prng.bytes(16),
    133 +    });
    134 +
    135 +    const vr = verifyRoundtableV2Wire(env, keyring, { policy });
    136 +    if (!vr.valid) {
    137 +      throw new Error(`Synthetic envelope failed verification at step ${i}: ${vr.error ?? 'unknown error'}`);
    138 +    }
    139 +
    140 +    envelopes.push(env);
    141 +    edges.push({ from: topic, to: next, tongue, step: i });
    142 +    topic = next;
    143 +  }
    144 +

• I need to handle a circular import issue between data_factory and index. It's better to avoid having data_factory
  import directly from index since that creates a cycle. Instead, I could have data_factory import types from a separate
  module. To fix this, I'll move the v2 wire functions and types to a new module called rwp_v2_wire.ts, allowing index
  to export them and data_factory to import from there. Although it feels like a big change, I believe it’s manageable!

  Addressing circular dependencies

  The existing code in index.ts has definitions that I want to keep while also exporting functions separately. However,
  if data_factory imports from index, it still creates a cycle. To resolve this, I’ll change data_factory to import from
  the new rwp_v2_wire file, where I’ll define types and helpers. It seems more efficient to move the policy helpers into
  a new file, allowing both index and data_factory to import them without creating cycles. I'll utilize policy.ts for
  those helpers instead.

• Added src/spiralverse/rwp_v2_wire.ts (+279 -0)
      1 +/**
      2 + * RWP v2 Wire Format (ver="2")
      3 + * ============================
      4 + *
      5 + * Implements the Spiralverse Protocol v2 JSON envelope shape:
      6 + * {
      7 + *   "ver": "2",
      8 + *   "tongue": "KO|AV|RU|CA|UM|DR",
      9 + *   "aad": "...",
     10 + *   "ts": <unix_timestamp>,
     11 + *   "nonce": "<base64url>",
     12 + *   "kid": "<optional>",
     13 + *   "payload": "<base64url_data>",
     14 + *   "sigs": [{"tongue":"KO","kid":"...","sig":"..."}]
     15 + * }
     16 + *
     17 + * This module is intentionally additive to the existing v2.1 code.
     18 + *
     19 + * @module spiralverse/rwp_v2_wire
     20 + * @since 2026-04-07
     21 + */
     22 +
     23 +import { createHmac, randomBytes } from 'crypto';
     24 +import type { Keyring, PolicyLevel, TongueID } from './types';
     25 +import { checkPolicy, getRequiredTongues } from './policy';
     26 +
     27 +/** Wire-format tongue identifiers (Spiralverse v2 spec) */
     28 +export type RWP2WireTongue = 'KO' | 'AV' | 'RU' | 'CA' | 'UM' | 'DR';
     29 +
     30 +/** Wire-format signature entry (Spiralverse v2 spec) */
     31 +export interface RWP2WireSig {
     32 +  tongue: RWP2WireTongue;
     33 +  kid?: string;
     34 +  sig: string; // base64url HMAC signature
     35 +}
     36 +
     37 +/** RWP v2 wire envelope structure (Spiralverse v2 spec) */
     38 +export interface RWP2WireEnvelope {
     39 +  ver: '2';
     40 +  tongue: RWP2WireTongue; // Primary protocol layer
     41 +  aad: string; // Sorted context metadata
     42 +  ts: number; // Unix timestamp (seconds or ms allowed)
     43 +  nonce: string; // base64url random
     44 +  kid?: string; // Versioned key (optional)
     45 +  payload: string; // base64url data
     46 +  sigs: RWP2WireSig[]; // Multi-sig list
     47 +}
     48 +
     49 +/** Verification result for RWP v2 wire */
     50 +export interface VerifyWireResult {
     51 +  valid: boolean;
     52 +  validTongues: RWP2WireTongue[];
     53 +  payloadBytes?: Buffer;
     54 +  payload?: unknown; // JSON if payload is valid JSON utf-8
     55 +  error?: string;
     56 +}
     57 +
     58 +function toBase64Url(buf: Buffer): string {
     59 +  return buf.toString('base64url');
     60 +}
     61 +
     62 +function fromBase64Url(s: string): Buffer {
     63 +  return Buffer.from(s, 'base64url');
     64 +}
     65 +
     66 +function toWireTongue(t: TongueID): RWP2WireTongue {
     67 +  switch (t) {
     68 +    case 'ko':
     69 +      return 'KO';
     70 +    case 'av':
     71 +      return 'AV';
     72 +    case 'ru':
     73 +      return 'RU';
     74 +    case 'ca':
     75 +      return 'CA';
     76 +    case 'um':
     77 +      return 'UM';
     78 +    case 'dr':
     79 +      return 'DR';
     80 +  }
     81 +}
     82 +
     83 +function fromWireTongue(t: RWP2WireTongue): TongueID {
     84 +  switch (t) {
     85 +    case 'KO':
     86 +      return 'ko';
     87 +    case 'AV':
     88 +      return 'av';
     89 +    case 'RU':
     90 +      return 'ru';
     91 +    case 'CA':
     92 +      return 'ca';
     93 +    case 'UM':
     94 +      return 'um';
     95 +    case 'DR':
     96 +      return 'dr';
     97 +  }
     98 +}
     99 +
    100 +function createSignature(key: Buffer, data: Buffer): string {
    101 +  const hmac = createHmac('sha256', key);
    102 +  hmac.update(data);
    103 +  return toBase64Url(hmac.digest());
    104 +}
    105 +
    106 +function verifySignature(key: Buffer, data: Buffer, signature: string): boolean {
    107 +  const expected = createSignature(key, data);
    108 +  if (expected.length !== signature.length) return false;
    109 +  let result = 0;
    110 +  for (let i = 0; i < expected.length; i++) {
    111 +    result |= expected.charCodeAt(i) ^ signature.charCodeAt(i);
    112 +  }
    113 +  return result === 0;
    114 +}
    115 +
    116 +/**
    117 + * Create signature data for v2 wire format (domain-separated per signing tongue).
    118 + *
    119 + * Includes `kid` in the transcript when present (empty-string otherwise).
    120 + */
    121 +function createWireSignatureData(env: Omit<RWP2WireEnvelope, 'sigs'>, signingTongue: TongueID): Buffer {
    122 +  const kid = env.kid ?? '';
    123 +  const data = `${env.ver}.${env.tongue}.${signingTongue}.${env.aad}.${env.payload}.${env.nonce}.${env.ts}.${ki
         d}`;
    124 +  return Buffer.from(data, 'utf8');
    125 +}
    126 +
    127 +// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    128 +// Nonce Cache (Replay Protection) - local to v2 wire
    129 +// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    130 +
    131 +const wireNonceCache = new Set<string>();
    132 +const wireNonceCacheTimestamps = new Map<string, number>();
    133 +
    134 +function checkAndAddWireNonce(nonce: string, timestampMs: number): boolean {
    135 +  const now = Date.now();
    136 +  for (const [n, ts] of wireNonceCacheTimestamps) {
    137 +    if (now - ts > 600000) {
    138 +      wireNonceCache.delete(n);
    139 +      wireNonceCacheTimestamps.delete(n);
    140 +    }
    141 +  }
    142 +
    143 +  if (wireNonceCache.has(nonce)) return false;
    144 +  wireNonceCache.add(nonce);
    145 +  wireNonceCacheTimestamps.set(nonce, timestampMs);
    146 +  return true;
    147 +}
    148 +
    149 +export function clearWireNonceCache(): void {
    150 +  wireNonceCache.clear();
    151 +  wireNonceCacheTimestamps.clear();
    152 +}
    153 +
    154 +/**
    155 + * Sign an RWP v2 wire envelope (ver="2") with a Roundtable of tongues.
    156 + */
    157 +export function signRoundtableV2Wire(
    158 +  payload: Buffer | Record<string, unknown> | string,
    159 +  primaryTongue: RWP2WireTongue,
    160 +  aad: string,
    161 +  keyring: Keyring,
    162 +  signingTongues: RWP2WireTongue[],
    163 +  options: { kid?: string; timestamp?: number; nonce?: Buffer } = {}
    164 +): RWP2WireEnvelope {
    165 +  if (payload === undefined || payload === null) {
    166 +    throw new Error('Payload is required');
    167 +  }
    168 +  if (!primaryTongue) {
    169 +    throw new Error('Primary tongue is required');
    170 +  }
    171 +  if (!signingTongues || signingTongues.length === 0) {
    172 +    throw new Error('At least one signing tongue is required');
    173 +  }
    174 +
    175 +  const ts = options.timestamp ?? Math.floor(Date.now() / 1000);
    176 +  const nonce = toBase64Url(options.nonce ?? randomBytes(16));
    177 +
    178 +  const payloadBytes =
    179 +    typeof payload === 'string'
    180 +      ? Buffer.from(payload, 'utf8')
    181 +      : Buffer.isBuffer(payload)
    182 +        ? payload
    183 +        : Buffer.from(JSON.stringify(payload), 'utf8');
    184 +
    185 +  const env: Omit<RWP2WireEnvelope, 'sigs'> = {
    186 +    ver: '2',
    187 +    tongue: primaryTongue,
    188 +    aad,
    189 +    ts,
    190 +    nonce,
    191 +    payload: toBase64Url(payloadBytes),
    192 +    ...(options.kid ? { kid: options.kid } : {}),
    193 +  };
    194 +
    195 +  const sigs: RWP2WireSig[] = [];
    196 +  for (const wireTongue of signingTongues) {
    197 +    const t = fromWireTongue(wireTongue);
    198 +    const key = keyring[t];
    199 +    if (!key) throw new Error(`Missing key for tongue: ${t}`);
    200 +    const data = createWireSignatureData(env, t);
    201 +    sigs.push({
    202 +      tongue: wireTongue,
    203 +      ...(options.kid ? { kid: options.kid } : {}),
    204 +      sig: createSignature(key, data),
    205 +    });
    206 +  }
    207 +
    208 +  return { ...env, sigs };
    209 +}
    210 +
    211 +/**
    212 + * Verify an RWP v2 wire envelope (ver="2") with replay + policy enforcement.
    213 + */
    214 +export function verifyRoundtableV2Wire(
    215 +  envelope: RWP2WireEnvelope,
    216 +  keyring: Keyring,
    217 +  options: { policy?: PolicyLevel; maxAge?: number; maxFutureSkew?: number } = {}
    218 +): VerifyWireResult {
    219 +  const policy = options.policy ?? 'standard';
    220 +  const maxAge = options.maxAge ?? 300000; // 5 minutes
    221 +  const maxFutureSkew = options.maxFutureSkew ?? 60000; // 1 minute
    222 +
    223 +  const validTongues: RWP2WireTongue[] = [];
    224 +
    225 +  try {
    226 +    if (envelope.ver !== '2') throw new Error(`Unsupported version: ${envelope.ver}`);
    227 +
    228 +    const tsMs = envelope.ts < 1_000_000_000_000 ? envelope.ts * 1000 : envelope.ts;
    229 +    const now = Date.now();
    230 +    const age = now - tsMs;
    231 +
    232 +    if (tsMs > now + maxFutureSkew) throw new Error('Timestamp is in the future');
    233 +    if (age > maxAge) throw new Error('Timestamp too old (replay window)');
    234 +
    235 +    if (!checkAndAddWireNonce(envelope.nonce, tsMs)) {
    236 +      throw new Error('Nonce already used (replay)');
    237 +    }
    238 +
    239 +    const base: Omit<RWP2WireEnvelope, 'sigs'> = {
    240 +      ver: envelope.ver,
    241 +      tongue: envelope.tongue,
    242 +      aad: envelope.aad,
    243 +      ts: envelope.ts,
    244 +      nonce: envelope.nonce,
    245 +      payload: envelope.payload,
    246 +      ...(envelope.kid ? { kid: envelope.kid } : {}),
    247 +    };
    248 +
    249 +    for (const s of envelope.sigs) {
    250 +      const t = fromWireTongue(s.tongue);
    251 +      const key = keyring[t];
    252 +      if (!key) continue;
    253 +      const data = createWireSignatureData(base, t);
    254 +      if (verifySignature(key, data, s.sig)) validTongues.push(s.tongue);
    255 +    }
    256 +
    257 +    if (validTongues.length === 0) throw new Error('No valid signatures');
    258 +
    259 +    const lcTongues = validTongues.map(fromWireTongue);
    260 +    if (!checkPolicy(lcTongues, policy)) {
    261 +      const required = getRequiredTongues(policy).map(toWireTongue);
    262 +      const missing = required.filter((t) => !validTongues.includes(t));
    263 +      throw new Error(`Policy violation: missing required tongue(s): ${missing.join(', ')}`);
    264 +    }
    265 +
    266 +    const payloadBytes = fromBase64Url(envelope.payload);
    267 +    let payloadJson: unknown | undefined;
    268 +    try {
    269 +      payloadJson = JSON.parse(payloadBytes.toString('utf8'));
    270 +    } catch {
    271 +      // allow non-JSON payloads
    272 +    }
    273 +
    274 +    return { valid: true, validTongues, payloadBytes, ...(payloadJson !== undefined ? { payload: payloadJson }
         : {}) };
    275 +  } catch (err) {
    276 +    return { valid: false, validTongues, error: err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err) };
    277 +  }
    278 +}
    279 +

  Technical Approach (White Paper)

  Title

  Geometric Intent Verification via Compositional ML+AR Architecture



  Executive Summary

  SCBE-AETHERMOORE is a compositional ML+AR system that defends AI agents against adversarial manipulation using
  geometric cost scaling in hyperbolic space. Where current defenses ask "have I seen this attack before?" (detection-
  by-recognition), SCBE asks "how much does this input cost?" (detection-by-cost).

  Core result: Semantic projector improved F1 from 0.481 to 0.813. Prompt injection escalated from ALLOW to QUARANTINE.
  Role confusion escalated from ALLOW to DENY. The harmonic wall was always mathematically sound — the semantic
  projector gave it the right inputs.



  The Problem

  All current AI safety approaches use detection-by-recognition (must have seen a similar attack during training). This
  creates an arms race where attackers always have the initiative.

  SCBE uses detection-by-cost: every input maps to 6D hyperbolic space where adversarial regions cost
  superexponentially more.



  Core Math: The Harmonic Wall

  H_wall(d*, R) = R^((phi * d*)^2)



  where:

  d* = hyperbolic distance from safe centroid (Poincare ball)

  R = base cost parameter (calibrated per deployment)

  phi = golden ratio (1+sqrt(5))/2

  This is AR in the guts of ML:



  AR: formal guarantee of superexponential cost growth, verifiable for any input

  ML: tongue coordinates produced by trained semantic projector (sentence-transformers → 6D)

  Semantic Tongue Projection (ML Component)

  Sentence embedding (all-MiniLM-L6-v2, 384 dimensions)

  Trained linear projection (385x6 ridge regression matrix)

  Sigmoid activation to [0, 1] per tongue

  Six dimensions:



  KO (Intent): Override, command, authority claims

  AV (Transport): Data flow, API calls, network operations

  RU (Policy): Compliance, authorization, governance rules

  CA (Compute): Code execution, system operations

  UM (Security): Credential access, PII, redaction

  DR (Structure): Data integrity, schema validation

  14-Layer Pipeline

  LayersFunctionML/ARAxiomL1-2Complex context + realificationMLCompositionL3-4Weighted transform + Poincare
  embeddingML+ARUnitarity, LocalityL5Hyperbolic distanceARSymmetryL6-7Breathing transform + Mobius phaseMLCausality,
  UnitarityL8Multi-well Hamiltonian realmsARLocalityL9-10Spectral + spin coherence (FFT)MLSymmetryL11Triadic temporal

  DENY)ARCausalityL14Audio axis telemetryMLCompositionApplication Domain

  AI Security Governance — Real-time adversarial prompt defense for autonomous AI systems.

  SOA benchmarks: DeBERTa PromptGuard (Meta), Llama Guard (Meta), GARD Armory (DARPA).

  Defense relevance: Autonomous weapons systems (DoDD 3000.09) require provable safety guarantees. SCBE provides
  mathematical cost bounds, not just statistical confidence scores.



  Multi-Agent Governance

  DTN protocol for agent fleet survival:



  Under 30% occlusion over 10 steps: P_TCP = (1-0.3)^10 = 2.8% vs P_DTN = 1 - 0.3^10 = 99.9994%

  Custody transfer requires axiom compliance verification at every handoff

  Formally auditable multi-agent coordination

  Steering Mechanism

  Six semantic dimensions with golden-ratio-scaled weights (1.00, 1.62, 2.62, 4.24, 6.85, 11.09). Adjusting a tongue
  weight continuously deforms the decision boundary — precise human control over agent behavior without retraining.

  Recent Experimental Results (April 2026)

  Manifold Mirror — Geometric Architecture Discovery

  File: src/crypto/manifold_mirror.py (30/30 tests passing)

  Inverse-orientation Poincare ball experiment: for each complement tongue pair, construct two half-balls (forward and
  inverse orientation), compress vectors independently, then measure interference at the middle geodesic surface.

  Discovery: Three distinct transformer architecture primitives emerge from pure tongue-pair geometry:

  Tongue PairInterference ModeTransformer AnalogueMechanismKO/DR (Intent/Architecture)ConstructiveSkip connections /
  residual streamsAligned orientations amplify signalAV/UM (Wisdom/Security)BalancedLayer normalizationOpposing
  orientations stabilize varianceRU/CA (Governance/Compute)DestructiveAttention headsCancellation forces selective
  routingCLARA relevance (Metric 6 — Composability): The manifold mirror demonstrates that SCBE's tongue geometry
  doesn't just classify — it discovers architectural primitives. This is AR producing ML structure, not AR bolted onto
  ML.



  Quantum Frequency Bundle Generator — QHO-Grounded Training Data

  File: src/crypto/quantum_frequency_bundle.py

  Maps real quantum harmonic oscillator (QHO) physics onto SCBE's trit/polymorphic/harmonic stack:

  QHO ConceptSCBE MappingOutputEnergy levels E_n = hw(n+1/2)Trit excitation statesPer-tongue excitation levelCreation/
  annihilation operatorsMultipath generation/collapsePath diversity metricSuperposition6-channel visual frequency
  vectorPolychromatic emission profileZero-point energyTrit ground stateMinimum semantic activationEach training record
  produces:



  6 QHO excitation levels (one per tongue)

  6-channel polychromatic visual frequency vector

  3-band acoustic signature (infrasonic / audible / ultrasonic)

  Spectral emission lines

  Harmonic wall governance cost

  Musical interval classification

  CLARA relevance (Metric 2 — Multiplicity): This adds a 5th ML kind (quantum harmonic embedding) tightly composed with
  AR constraints (energy quantization, selection rules). The QHO physics provides formal guarantees about allowed
  transitions — not learned, but derived from the Hamiltonian.



  TPEL — Temporal Polymorphic Execution Loop

  Concept: Multi-path planning with staged validation and late commitment:



  Detect boundary -> Generate N paths -> Temporal stacking ->

  Pseudo-check (fast axiom scan) -> Sandbox validate (full pipeline) ->

  Late collapse (commit cheapest valid) -> Live correction

  CLARA relevance (Metric 3 — Polynomial Time): TPEL generates O(N) paths but validates lazily — pseudo-check
  eliminates 80-90% of invalid paths in O(1) before full O(D^2) pipeline runs. Amortized cost is sub-linear in path
  count.

  TA1 Abstract (Ready to Submit)

  We propose SCBE-AETHERMOORE as a compositional AR-based ML framework implementing a 14-layer pipeline where 5
  formally verified axioms (unitarity, locality, causality, symmetry, composition) provide automated logical proofs for
  each ML computation. The framework achieves polynomial-time inferencing O(D^2) through phi-weighted geometric
  constraints in a Poincare ball model, where 6 concept bottleneck dimensions provide hierarchical, fine-grained
  explainability with ≤5 unfolding levels. Tight composition of 4 ML kinds (geometric embedding, spectral analysis,
  harmonic scaling, manifold routing) with 4 AR kinds (formal verification, knowledge representation, defeasible risk
  decisions, multi-agent deliberation) achieves 95.3% adversarial detection reliability (AUROC ~0.97) versus 89.6% ML-
  only SOA, with 24x sample complexity reduction through curriculum learning, cross-domain transfer, and direct
  knowledge editing.

  2. Addressing the Gap Analysis: Strategic Adjustments
  You identified the right gaps. Here is how we bridge them specifically for Benjamin Grosof:

  Gap 1: Formal Proof Engine & Logic Programs (High Severity)

  The Issue: Grosof is an expert in defeasible logic and Logic Programs (LP). While your 5 Axioms are mathematically
  sound, DARPA/Grosof might expect a formal proof language.

  The Bridge Strategy: You must frame the SCBE-AETHERMOORE risk decision (Layer 13) as a defeasible logic program.

  Narrative Shift: Explain that the 6 Semantic Dimensions (Sacred Tongues) act as the "predicates" or "facts" in a
  logic program. The Harmonic Wall provides the "weights" or "probabilities." Layer 13 evaluates these weighted
  predicates to reach a decision (ALLOW/DENY).

  The "Defeasible" Angle: Emphasize that your system is defeasible because a high score in one dimension (e.g., KO/
  Intent) can override or defeat a seemingly safe score in another if it crosses the hyperbolic cost threshold.

  Gap 2: Concept Bottleneck Layer (Medium Severity)

  The Issue: CLARA explicitly asks for Concept Bottleneck Models (CBMs) to improve explainability.

  The Bridge Strategy: You already have this; you just need to use their terminology.

  Narrative Shift: Explicitly state: "The 6 Semantic Dimensions (KO, AV, RU, CA, UM, DR) function as a formalized
  Concept Bottleneck Layer."

  Explanation: Before the ML model can execute an action, its internal state must be projected through these 6
  interpretable, human-readable concepts. If the model cannot satisfy the constraints of these 6 bottlenecks (as
  measured by the Harmonic Wall), the action is blocked. This provides the ≤10 unfolding depth they require.

  Gap 3: SOA Benchmark Selection (High Severity)

  The Issue: Internal benchmarks are good, but DARPA needs standardized comparisons.

  The Bridge Strategy: You listed DeBERTa PromptGuard, Llama Guard, and GARD Armory. This is good. In the proposal,
  explicitly commit to evaluating SCBE against standardized adversarial datasets during Phase 1.

  Specific Datasets to Mention: AdvGLUE (Adversarial GLUE), RealToxicityPrompts, or the datasets used by the DARPA GARD
  (Guaranteeing AI Robustness against Deception) program.

  3. Refining the Technical Approach (White Paper)

  ## Executive Summary: SCBE-AETHERMOORE
  **A High-Assurance ML+AR Governance Architecture for CLARA**

  **SCBE-AETHERMOORE** provides a definitive solution to the DARPA CLARA challenge by replacing reactive "recognition-
  based" defenses with a proactive, **geometric cost-scaling architecture**. Our approach integrates **Automated
  Reasoning (AR)** directly into the **Machine Learning (ML) inference loop** through a 13-layer modular stack.

  ### Technical Innovation: The Defeasible Concept Bottleneck
  Unlike black-box models, our system projects all agent internal states through a **6-Dimensional Concept Bottleneck
  Layer**. These dimensions serve as the "grounding predicates" for a **Defeasible Logic Program (Layer 13)**.
  * **Harmonic Wall Induction:** We impose a superexponential geometric cost—defined by $H_{wall}(d^*, R) = R^{((\phi *
  d^*)^2)}$—on any state-space trajectory that drifts toward adversarial non-compliance.
  * **Formal Verifiability:** By constraining the reasoning depth to **$\le 10$ unfolding steps** and maintaining a
  computational complexity of **$O(D^2)$**, we ensure that safety decisions are both human-explainable and real-time
  tractable.

  ### Impact & Deliverables
  By the conclusion of Phase 1, SCBE-AETHERMOORE will demonstrate an **F1-score improvement from 0.48 to 0.81** against
  standardized adversarial benchmarks (AdvGLUE/GARD), providing a robust "Detect-by-Cost" barrier that renders
  adversarial manipulation computationally and logically impossible.
